</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed machine-learning-list-title"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="border-top:1px solid #aaa; text-align:center;background-color:#e0e0e0;;color: var(--color-base)">Related articles</div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_artificial_intelligence" title="Glossary of artificial intelligence">Glossary of artificial intelligence</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_datasets_for_machine-learning_research" title="List of datasets for machine-learning research">List of datasets for machine-learning research</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_datasets_in_computer_vision_and_image_processing" title="List of datasets in computer vision and image processing">List of datasets in computer vision and image processing</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_machine_learning" title="Outline of machine learning">Outline of machine learning</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239400231" /><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Machine_learning" title="Template:Machine learning"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Machine_learning" title="Template talk:Machine learning"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Machine_learning" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Machine learning"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Statistical_model" title="Statistical model">statistical modeling</a>, <b>regression analysis</b> is a statistical method for <a href="/wiki/Estimation_theory" title="Estimation theory">estimating</a> the relationship between a <a href="/wiki/Dependent_variable" class="mw-redirect" title="Dependent variable">dependent variable</a> (often called the <i>outcome</i> or <i>response</i> variable, or a <i>label</i> in machine learning parlance) and one or more <a href="/wiki/Independent_variable" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent variable">independent variables</a> (often called <i>regressors</i>, <i>predictors</i>, <i>covariates</i>, <i>explanatory variables</i> or <i>features</i>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The most common form of regression analysis is <a href="/wiki/Linear_regression" title="Linear regression">linear regression</a>, in which one finds the line (or a more complex <a href="/wiki/Linear_combination" title="Linear combination">linear combination</a>) that most closely fits the data according to a specific mathematical criterion. For example, the method of <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_least_squares" title="Ordinary least squares">ordinary least squares</a> computes the unique line (or <a href="/wiki/Hyperplane" title="Hyperplane">hyperplane</a>) that minimizes the sum of squared differences between the true data and that line (or hyperplane). For specific mathematical reasons (see <a href="/wiki/Linear_regression" title="Linear regression">linear regression</a>), this allows the researcher to estimate the <a href="/wiki/Conditional_expectation" title="Conditional expectation">conditional expectation</a> (or population <a href="/wiki/Average_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Average value">average value</a>) of the dependent variable when the independent variables take on a given set of values. Less common forms of regression use slightly different procedures to estimate alternative <a href="/wiki/Location_parameters" class="mw-redirect" title="Location parameters">location parameters</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Quantile_regression" title="Quantile regression">quantile regression</a> or <a href="/wiki/Necessary_Condition_Analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Necessary Condition Analysis">Necessary Condition Analysis</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) or estimate the conditional expectation across a broader collection of non-linear models (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Nonparametric_regression" title="Nonparametric regression">nonparametric regression</a>).
</p><p>Regression analysis is primarily used for two conceptually distinct purposes. First, regression analysis is widely used for <a href="/wiki/Prediction" title="Prediction">prediction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forecasting" title="Forecasting">forecasting</a>, where its use has substantial overlap with the field of <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a>. Second, in some situations regression analysis can be used to infer <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causal relationships</a> between the independent and dependent variables. Importantly, regressions by themselves only reveal relationships between a dependent variable and a collection of independent variables in a fixed dataset. To use regressions for prediction or to infer causal relationships, respectively, a researcher must carefully justify why existing relationships have predictive power for a new context or why a relationship between two variables has a causal interpretation. The latter is especially important when researchers hope to estimate causal relationships using <a href="/wiki/Observational_study" title="Observational study">observational data</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Freedman2009&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedman2009-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The earliest regression form was seen in <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>'s work in 1700 while studying <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinoxes</a>, being credited with introducing "an embryonic linear regression analysis" as "not only did he perform the averaging of a set of data, 50 years before <a href="/wiki/Tobias_Mayer" title="Tobias Mayer">Tobias Mayer</a>, but by summing the residuals to zero he <i>forced</i> the regression line to pass through the average point. He also distinguished between two inhomogeneous sets of data and might have thought of an <i>optimal</i> solution in terms of bias, though not in terms of effectiveness."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He previously used an averaging method in his 1671 work on <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_rings" title="Newton&#39;s rings">Newton's rings</a>, which was unprecedented at the time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Method_of_least_squares" class="mw-redirect" title="Method of least squares">method of least squares</a> was published by <a href="/wiki/Adrien-Marie_Legendre" title="Adrien-Marie Legendre">Legendre</a> in 1805,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Legendre&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legendre-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Gauss</a> in 1809.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gauss&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gauss-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Legendre and Gauss both applied the method to the problem of determining, from astronomical observations, the orbits of bodies about the Sun (mostly comets, but also later the then newly discovered minor planets). Gauss published a further development of the theory of least squares in 1821,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gauss2&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gauss2-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> including a version of the <a href="/wiki/Gauss%E2%80%93Markov_theorem" title="Gauss–Markov theorem">Gauss–Markov theorem</a>.
</p><p>The term "regression" was coined by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Galton" title="Francis Galton">Francis Galton</a> in the 19th century to describe a biological phenomenon. The phenomenon was that the heights of descendants of tall ancestors tend to regress down towards a normal average (a phenomenon also known as <a href="/wiki/Regression_toward_the_mean" title="Regression toward the mean">regression toward the mean</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
For Galton, regression had only this biological meaning,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but his work was later extended by <a href="/wiki/Udny_Yule" title="Udny Yule">Udny Yule</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Pearson" title="Karl Pearson">Karl Pearson</a> to a more general statistical context.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the work of Yule and Pearson, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint distribution">joint distribution</a> of the response and explanatory variables is assumed to be <a href="/wiki/Normal_distribution" title="Normal distribution">Gaussian</a>. This assumption was weakened by <a href="/wiki/Ronald_A._Fisher" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronald A. Fisher">R.A. Fisher</a> in his works of 1922 and 1925.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FisherR1954Statistical&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FisherR1954Statistical-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fisher assumed that the <a href="/wiki/Conditional_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Conditional distribution">conditional distribution</a> of the response variable is Gaussian, but the joint distribution need not be. In this respect, Fisher's assumption is closer to Gauss's formulation of 1821.
</p><p>In the 1950s and 1960s, economists used <a href="/wiki/Calculator#Precursors_to_the_electronic_calculator" title="Calculator">electromechanical desk calculators</a> to calculate regressions. Before 1970, it sometimes took up to 24 hours to receive the result from one regression.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Regression methods continue to be an area of active research. In recent decades, new methods have been developed for <a href="/wiki/Robust_regression" title="Robust regression">robust regression</a>, regression involving correlated responses such as <a href="/wiki/Time_series" title="Time series">time series</a> and <a href="/wiki/Growth_curve_(statistics)" title="Growth curve (statistics)">growth curves</a>, regression in which the predictor (independent variable) or response variables are curves, images, graphs, or other complex data objects, regression methods accommodating various types of missing data, <a href="/wiki/Nonparametric_regression" title="Nonparametric regression">nonparametric regression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_statistics" title="Bayesian statistics">Bayesian</a> methods for regression, regression in which the predictor variables are measured with error, regression with more predictor variables than observations, and <a href="/wiki/Causal_inference" title="Causal inference">causal inference</a> with regression. Modern regression analysis is typically done with statistical and <a href="/wiki/Spreadsheet" title="Spreadsheet">spreadsheet</a> software packages on computers as well as on handheld <a href="/wiki/Scientific_calculator" title="Scientific calculator">scientific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graphing_calculator" title="Graphing calculator">graphing calculators</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regression_model">Regression model</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Regression model"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In practice, researchers first select a model they would like to estimate and then use their chosen method (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_least_squares" title="Ordinary least squares">ordinary least squares</a>) to estimate the parameters of that model. Regression models involve the following components:
</p>
<ul><li>The <b>unknown parameters</b>, often denoted as a <a href="/wiki/Scalar_(physics)" title="Scalar (physics)">scalar</a> or <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_vector" title="Euclidean vector">vector</a> <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \beta }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \beta }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ed48a5e36207156fb792fa79d29925d2f7901e8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.332ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \beta }"></span>.</li>
<li>The <b>independent variables</b>, which are observed in data and are often denoted as a vector <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af4a0955af42beb5f85aa05fb8c07abedc13990d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.724ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X_{i}}"></span> (where <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle i}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>i</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle i}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/add78d8608ad86e54951b8c8bd6c8d8416533d20" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.802ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle i}"></span> denotes a row of data).</li>
<li>The <b>dependent variable</b>, which are observed in data and often denoted using the scalar <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Y_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

          <mi>Y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d57be496fff95ee2a97ee43c7f7fe244b4dbf8ae" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.15ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle Y_{i}}"></span>.</li>
<li>The <b>error terms</b>, which are <i>not</i> directly observed in data and are often denoted using the scalar <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span>.</li></ul>
<p>In various <a href="/wiki/List_of_fields_of_application_of_statistics" title="List of fields of application of statistics">fields of application</a>, different terminologies are used in place of <a href="/wiki/Dependent_and_independent_variables" title="Dependent and independent variables">dependent and independent variables</a>.
</p><p>Most regression models propose that <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Y_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Y_{i}=f(X_{i},\beta )+e_{i}}">

<p>In the standard regression model, the independent variables <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af4a0955af42beb5f85aa05fb8c07abedc13990d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.724ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X_{i}}"></span> are assumed to be free of error. The <a href="/wiki/Errors-in-variables_model" title="Errors-in-variables model">errors-in-variables model</a> can be used if the independent variables are assumed to contain errors. Other modifications to the standard regression model can be made to account for various scenarios, such as situations involving <a href="/wiki/Omitted_variable_bias" class="mw-redirect" title="Omitted variable bias">omitted variables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confounder" class="mw-redirect" title="Confounder">confounding variables</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endogeneity_(econometrics)" title="Endogeneity (econometrics)">endogeneity</a>. 
</p><p>The researchers' goal is to estimate the function <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f(X_{i},\beta )}">

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>f</mi>

            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>

To carry out regression analysis, the form of the function <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f}">

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle f}"></span> must be specified. Sometimes the form of this function is based on knowledge about the relationship between <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Y_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

            <mi>i</mi>

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d57be496fff95ee2a97ee43c7f7fe244b4dbf8ae" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.15ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle Y_{i}}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X_{i}}">
  <semantics>

If no such knowledge is available, a flexible or convenient form for <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f}">

For example, a simple univariate regression may propose <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f(X_{i},\beta )=\beta _{0}+\beta _{1}X_{i}}">

</p><p>Once researchers determine their preferred <a href="/wiki/Statistical_model" title="Statistical model">statistical model</a>, different forms of regression analysis provide tools to estimate the parameters <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \beta }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \beta }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ed48a5e36207156fb792fa79d29925d2f7901e8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.332ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \beta }"></span>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Least_squares" title="Least squares">least squares</a> (including its most common variant, <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_least_squares" title="Ordinary least squares">ordinary least squares</a>) finds the value of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \beta }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \beta }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ed48a5e36207156fb792fa79d29925d2f7901e8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.332ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \beta }"></span> that minimizes the sum of squared errors <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{i}(Y_{i}-f(X_{i},\beta ))^{2}}">
  <semantics>

            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <msup>
          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

Whether the researcher is intrinsically interested in the estimate <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {\beta }}}">

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {Y}}_{i}={\hat {\beta }}_{0}+{\hat {\beta }}_{1}X_{1i}+{\hat {\beta }}_{2}X_{2i}}</annotation>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2aff00a186f849e413d57b38b6c7e9688e11a35c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:25.961ex; height:3.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\hat {Y}}_{i}={\hat {\beta }}_{0}+{\hat {\beta }}_{1}X_{1i}+{\hat {\beta }}_{2}X_{2i}}"></span>, all of which lead to <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{i}{\hat {e}}_{i}^{2}=\sum _{i}({\hat {Y}}_{i}-({\hat {\beta }}_{0}+{\hat {\beta }}_{1}X_{1i}+{\hat {\beta }}_{2}X_{2i}))^{2}=0}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

        <mn>0</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{i}{\hat {e}}_{i}^{2}=\sum _{i}({\hat {Y}}_{i}-({\hat {\beta }}_{0}+{\hat {\beta }}_{1}X_{1i}+{\hat {\beta }}_{2}X_{2i}))^{2}=0}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4f20256b69f245c8dc4fc5b5aca524743e81e7b3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:47.178ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{i}{\hat {e}}_{i}^{2}=\sum _{i}({\hat {Y}}_{i}-({\hat {\beta }}_{0}+{\hat {\beta }}_{1}X_{1i}+{\hat {\beta }}_{2}X_{2i}))^{2}=0}"></span> and are therefore valid solutions that minimize the sum of squared <a href="/wiki/Errors_and_residuals" title="Errors and residuals">residuals</a>. To understand why there are infinitely many options, note that the system of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N=2}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>2</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N=2}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/405d64b14536deffc3465f1e81b1b7fe9358ad2a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.325ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N=2}"></span> equations is to be solved for 3 unknowns, which makes the system <a href="/wiki/Underdetermined_system" title="Underdetermined system">underdetermined</a>. Alternatively, one can visualize infinitely many 3-dimensional planes that go through <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N=2}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>2</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N=2}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/405d64b14536deffc3465f1e81b1b7fe9358ad2a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.325ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N=2}"></span> fixed points.
</p><p>More generally, to estimate a <a href="/wiki/Least_squares" title="Least squares">least squares</a> model with <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle k}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>k</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle k}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3c9a2c7b599b37105512c5d570edc034056dd40" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.211ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle k}"></span> distinct parameters, one must have <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N\geq k}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>&#x2265;<!-- ≥ --></mo>
        <mi>k</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N\geq k}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1c196ee1648b059f8d29d3d73bc9231abc2f9079" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:6.373ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N\geq k}"></span> distinct data points. If <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N&gt;k}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>&gt;</mo>
        <mi>k</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N&gt;k}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/59092840ba8257fc7356c8e2fe7bb155d17bab04" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.373ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N&gt;k}"></span>, then there does not generally exist a set of parameters that will perfectly fit the data. The quantity <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N-k}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mi>k</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N-k}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b2be1ed483f56ec7456f3c17c567322141ca452" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:6.115ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N-k}"></span> appears often in regression analysis, and is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_freedom_(statistics)" title="Degrees of freedom (statistics)">degrees of freedom</a> in the model. Moreover, to estimate a least squares model, the independent variables <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (X_{1i},X_{2i},...,X_{ki})}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>k</mi>
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (X_{1i},X_{2i},...,X_{ki})}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1e09f1468c41c1f62e17a256f902fddca414758" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.685ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (X_{1i},X_{2i},...,X_{ki})}"></span> must be <a href="/wiki/Linear_independence" title="Linear independence">linearly independent</a>: one must <i>not</i> be able to reconstruct any of the independent variables by adding and multiplying the remaining independent variables. As discussed in <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_least_squares" title="Ordinary least squares">ordinary least squares</a>, this condition ensures that <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X^{T}X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>T</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X^{T}X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1cf126839e1552c18f9c9951a9267bee93f3d243" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.366ex; height:2.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X^{T}X}"></span> is an <a href="/wiki/Invertible_matrix" title="Invertible matrix">invertible matrix</a> and therefore that a unique solution <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {\beta }}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mover>
              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">&#x005E;<!-- ^ --></mo>
            </mover>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {\beta }}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/efdb50e00928e4013750a476dab75eeb3cbd5799" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.451ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\hat {\beta }}}"></span> exists.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Underlying_assumptions">Underlying assumptions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Underlying assumptions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<p>By itself, a regression is just a computation performed on a set of data. In order to interpret the resultant regression as a meaningful statistical model that quantifies real-world relationships, researchers often rely on a number of classical <a href="/wiki/Statistical_assumption" title="Statistical assumption">assumptions</a>. These assumptions often include:
</p>
<ul><li>The sample is representative of the population at large.</li>
<li>The independent variables are measured without error.</li>
<li>Deviations from the model have an expected value of zero, conditional on covariates: <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle E(e_{i}|X_{i})=0}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>E</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
        </mrow>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>0</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E(e_{i}|X_{i})=0}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0fecb384df3e2fb0dbafb2422a550fa0d7b21405" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.1ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle E(e_{i}|X_{i})=0}"></span></li>
<li>The variance of the residuals <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span> is constant across observations (<a href="/wiki/Homoscedasticity" class="mw-redirect" title="Homoscedasticity">homoscedasticity</a>).</li>
<li>The residuals <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span> are <a href="/wiki/Uncorrelated" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncorrelated">uncorrelated</a> with one another. Mathematically, the <a href="/wiki/Covariance_matrix" title="Covariance matrix">variance–covariance matrix</a> of the errors is <a href="/wiki/Diagonal_matrix" title="Diagonal matrix">diagonal</a>.</li></ul>
<p>A handful of conditions are sufficient for the least-squares estimator to possess desirable properties: in particular, the <a href="/wiki/Gauss%E2%80%93Markov_theorem" title="Gauss–Markov theorem">Gauss–Markov</a> assumptions imply that the parameter estimates will be <a href="/wiki/Bias_of_an_estimator" title="Bias of an estimator">unbiased</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consistent_estimator" title="Consistent estimator">consistent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Efficient_(statistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Efficient (statistics)">efficient</a> in the class of linear unbiased estimators. Practitioners have developed a variety of methods to maintain some or all of these desirable properties in real-world settings, because these classical assumptions are unlikely to hold exactly. For example, modeling <a href="/wiki/Errors-in-variables_model" title="Errors-in-variables model">errors-in-variables</a> can lead to reasonable estimates independent variables are measured with errors. <a href="/wiki/Heteroscedasticity-consistent_standard_errors" class="mw-redirect" title="Heteroscedasticity-consistent standard errors">Heteroscedasticity-consistent standard errors</a> allow the variance of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span> to change across values of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af4a0955af42beb5f85aa05fb8c07abedc13990d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.724ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X_{i}}"></span>. Correlated errors that exist within subsets of the data or follow specific patterns can be handled using <i>clustered standard errors, geographic weighted regression</i>, or <a href="/wiki/Newey%E2%80%93West_estimator" title="Newey–West estimator">Newey–West</a> standard errors, among other techniques. When rows of data correspond to locations in space, the choice of how to model <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span> within geographic units can have important consequences.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The subfield of <a href="/wiki/Econometrics" title="Econometrics">econometrics</a> is largely focused on developing techniques that allow researchers to make reasonable real-world conclusions in real-world settings, where classical assumptions do not hold exactly.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Linear_regression">Linear regression</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Linear regression"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Linear_regression" title="Linear regression">Linear regression</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See <a href="/wiki/Simple_linear_regression" title="Simple linear regression">simple linear regression</a> for a derivation of these formulas and a numerical example</div>
<p>In linear regression, the model specification is that the dependent variable, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y_{i}}">

    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

    </mrow>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/67d30d30b6c2dbe4d6f150d699de040937ecc95f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.939ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y_{i}}"></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Linear_combination" title="Linear combination">linear combination</a> of the <i>parameters</i> (but need not be linear in the <i>independent variables</i>). For example, in <a href="/wiki/Simple_linear_regression" title="Simple linear regression">simple linear regression</a> for modeling <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle n}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/00e1b6ad3cbad4af49bf21a3ad2dc379ff045079" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \varepsilon _{i}}"></span> is an error term and the subscript <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle i}">

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>i</mi>
      </mstyle>

  </semantics>

</p><p>Returning our attention to the straight line case: Given a random sample from the population, we estimate the population parameters and obtain the sample linear regression model:

One method of estimation is <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_least_squares" title="Ordinary least squares">ordinary least squares</a>. This method obtains parameter estimates that minimize the sum of squared <a href="/wiki/Errors_and_residuals_in_statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Errors and residuals in statistics">residuals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Residual_sum_of_squares" title="Residual sum of squares">SSR</a>:

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle SSR=\sum _{i=1}^{n}e_{i}^{2}}">

<p>Minimization of this function results in a set of <a href="/wiki/Linear_least_squares_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Linear least squares (mathematics)">normal equations</a>, a set of simultaneous linear equations in the parameters, which are solved to yield the parameter estimators, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\widehat {\beta }}_{0},{\widehat {\beta }}_{1}}">

<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\bar {x}}}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/466e03e1c9533b4dab1b9949dad393883f385d80" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\bar {x}}}"></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_mean" title="Arithmetic mean">mean</a> (average) of the <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">

</p><p>Under the assumption that the population error term has a constant variance, the estimate of that variance is given by:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {\sigma }}_{\varepsilon }^{2}={\frac {SSR}{n-2}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>S</mi>
              <mi>S</mi>
              <mi>R</mi>
            </mrow>

<p>This is called the <a href="/wiki/Mean_square_error" class="mw-redirect" title="Mean square error">mean square error</a> (MSE) of the regression. The denominator is the sample size reduced by the number of model parameters estimated from the same data, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (n-p)}">

<p>Under the further assumption that the population error term is normally distributed, the researcher can use these estimated standard errors to create <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval" title="Confidence interval">confidence intervals</a> and conduct <a href="/wiki/Hypothesis_test" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypothesis test">hypothesis tests</a> about the <a href="/wiki/Population_parameter" class="mw-redirect" title="Population parameter">population parameters</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="General_linear_model">General linear model</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: General linear model"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2f461e54f5c093e92a55547b9764291390f0b5d0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.027ex; width:0.985ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle j}"></span>-th independent variable.
If the first independent variable takes the value 1 for all <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle i}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/add78d8608ad86e54951b8c8bd6c8d8416533d20" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.802ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle i}"></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x_{i1}=1}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
      </mstyle>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e29706788693b7f680e4d6dd2cfd96078cd968d8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.212ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x_{i1}=1}"></span>, then <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \beta _{1}}">

</p><p>The least squares parameter estimates are obtained from <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p}">

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Diagnostics">Diagnostics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Diagnostics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regression_diagnostics" class="mw-redirect" title="Regression diagnostics">Regression diagnostics</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Regression_diagnostics" title="Category:Regression diagnostics">Category:Regression diagnostics</a></div>
<p>Once a regression model has been constructed, it may be important to confirm the <a href="/wiki/Goodness_of_fit" title="Goodness of fit">goodness of fit</a> of the model and the <a href="/wiki/Statistical_significance" title="Statistical significance">statistical significance</a> of the estimated parameters. Commonly used checks of goodness of fit include the <a href="/wiki/R-squared" class="mw-redirect" title="R-squared">R-squared</a>, analyses of the pattern of <a href="/wiki/Errors_and_residuals_in_statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Errors and residuals in statistics">residuals</a> and hypothesis testing. Statistical significance can be checked by an <a href="/wiki/F-test" title="F-test">F-test</a> of the overall fit, followed by <a href="/wiki/T-test" class="mw-redirect" title="T-test">t-tests</a> of individual parameters.
</p><p>Interpretations of these diagnostic tests rest heavily on the model's assumptions. Although examination of the residuals can be used to invalidate a model, the results of a <a href="/wiki/T-test" class="mw-redirect" title="T-test">t-test</a> or <a href="/wiki/F-test" title="F-test">F-test</a> are sometimes more difficult to interpret if the model's assumptions are violated. For example, if the error term does not have a normal distribution, in small samples the estimated parameters will not follow normal distributions and complicate inference. With relatively large samples, however, a <a href="/wiki/Central_limit_theorem" title="Central limit theorem">central limit theorem</a> can be invoked such that hypothesis testing may proceed using asymptotic approximations.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Limited_dependent_variables">Limited dependent variables</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Limited dependent variables"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Limited_dependent_variable" title="Limited dependent variable">Limited dependent variables</a>, which are response variables that are <a href="/wiki/Categorical_variable" title="Categorical variable">categorical</a> or constrained to fall only in a certain range, often arise in <a href="/wiki/Econometrics" title="Econometrics">econometrics</a>.
</p><p>The response variable may be non-continuous ("limited" to lie on some subset of the real line). For binary (zero or one) variables, if analysis proceeds with least-squares linear regression, the model is called the <a href="/wiki/Linear_probability_model" title="Linear probability model">linear probability model</a>. Nonlinear models for binary dependent variables include the <a href="/wiki/Probit_model" title="Probit model">probit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logistic_regression" title="Logistic regression">logit model</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Multivariate_probit" class="mw-redirect" title="Multivariate probit">multivariate probit</a> model is a standard method of estimating a joint relationship between several binary dependent variables and some independent variables. For <a href="/wiki/Categorical_variable" title="Categorical variable">categorical variables</a> with more than two values there is the <a href="/wiki/Multinomial_logit" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinomial logit">multinomial logit</a>. For <a href="/wiki/Ordinal_variable" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinal variable">ordinal variables</a> with more than two values, there are the <a href="/wiki/Ordered_logit" title="Ordered logit">ordered logit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ordered_probit" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordered probit">ordered probit</a> models. <a href="/wiki/Censored_regression_model" title="Censored regression model">Censored regression models</a> may be used when the dependent variable is only sometimes observed, and <a href="/wiki/Heckman_correction" title="Heckman correction">Heckman correction</a> type models may be used when the sample is not randomly selected from the population of interest. 
</p><p>An alternative to such procedures is linear regression based on <a href="/wiki/Polychoric_correlation" title="Polychoric correlation">polychoric correlation</a> (or polyserial correlations) between the categorical variables. Such procedures differ in the assumptions made about the distribution of the variables in the population. If the variable is positive with low values and represents the repetition of the occurrence of an event, then count models like the <a href="/wiki/Poisson_regression" title="Poisson regression">Poisson regression</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Negative_binomial" class="mw-redirect" title="Negative binomial">negative binomial</a> model may be used.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Nonlinear_regression">Nonlinear regression</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nonlinear regression"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_regression" title="Nonlinear regression">Nonlinear regression</a></div>
<p>When the model function is not linear in the parameters, the sum of squares must be minimized by an iterative procedure. This introduces many complications which are summarized in <a href="/wiki/Least_squares#Differences_between_linear_and_nonlinear_least_squares" title="Least squares">Differences between linear and non-linear least squares</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Prediction_(interpolation_and_extrapolation)"><span id="Prediction_.28interpolation_and_extrapolation.29"></span>Prediction (interpolation and extrapolation) <span class="anchor" id="Prediction"></span><span class="anchor" id="Interpolation"></span><span class="anchor" id="Extrapolation"></span><span class="anchor" id="Interpolation&#95;and&#95;extrapolation"></span></h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Prediction (interpolation and extrapolation)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Predicted_response" class="mw-redirect" title="Predicted response">Predicted response</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prediction_interval" title="Prediction interval">Prediction interval</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CurveWeightHeight.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/CurveWeightHeight.png/500px-CurveWeightHeight.png" decoding="async" width="380" height="234" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/CurveWeightHeight.png/960px-CurveWeightHeight.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1199" data-file-height="737" /></a><figcaption>In the middle, the fitted straight line represents the best balance between the points above and below this line. The dotted straight lines represent the two extreme lines, considering only the variation in the slope. The inner curves represent the estimated range of values considering the variation in both slope and intercept. The outer curves represent a prediction for a new measurement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Regression models <i><b>predict</b></i> a value of the <i>Y</i> variable given known values of the <i>X</i> variables. Prediction <em>within</em> the range of values in the dataset used for model-fitting is known informally as <i><a href="/wiki/Interpolation" title="Interpolation">interpolation</a></i>. Prediction <em>outside</em> this range of the data is known as <i><a href="/wiki/Extrapolation" title="Extrapolation">extrapolation</a></i>. Performing extrapolation relies strongly on the regression assumptions. The further the extrapolation goes outside the data, the more room there is for the model to fail due to differences between the assumptions and the sample data or the true values.
</p><p>A <i><a href="/wiki/Prediction_interval" title="Prediction interval">prediction interval</a></i> that represents the uncertainty may accompany the point prediction. Such intervals tend to expand rapidly as the values of the independent variable(s) moved outside the range covered by the observed data.
</p><p>For such reasons and others, some tend to say that it might be unwise to undertake extrapolation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Model_selection">Model selection</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Model selection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Model_selection" title="Model selection">Model selection</a></div>
<p>The assumption of a particular form for the relation between <i>Y</i> and <i>X</i> is another source of uncertainty. A properly conducted regression analysis will include an assessment of how well the assumed form is matched by the observed data, but it can only do so within the range of values of the independent variables actually available. This means that any extrapolation is particularly reliant on the assumptions being made about the structural form of the regression relationship. If this knowledge includes the fact that the dependent variable cannot go outside a certain range of values, this can be made use of in selecting the model – even if the observed dataset has no values particularly near such bounds. The implications of this step of choosing an appropriate functional form for the regression can be great when extrapolation is considered. At a minimum, it can ensure that any extrapolation arising from a fitted model is "realistic" (or in accord with what is known).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Power_and_sample_size_calculations">Power and sample size calculations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Power and sample size calculations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are no generally agreed methods for relating the number of observations versus the number of independent variables in the model. One method conjectured by Good and Hardin is <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N=m^{n}}">

            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5e3890c981ae85503089652feb48b191b57aae3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle N}"></span> is the sample size, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle n}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle n}"></span> is the number of independent variables and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle m}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>m</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle m}"></span> is the number of observations needed to reach the desired precision if the model had only one independent variable.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, a researcher is building a linear regression model using a dataset that contains 1000 patients (<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N}">

If the researcher decides that five observations are needed to precisely define a straight line (<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle m}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>m</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle m}"></span>), then the maximum number of independent variables (<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle n}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>n</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle n}"></span>) the model can support is 4, because
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {\log 1000}{\log 5}}\approx 4.29}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>log</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mn>1000</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>log</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mn>5</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x2248;<!-- ≈ --></mo>
        <mn>4.29</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {\log 1000}{\log 5}}\approx 4.29}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b5d9e5574ecd7e12c0c2265b31fdb2511d8882b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:16.077ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {\log 1000}{\log 5}}\approx 4.29}"></span>.</dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Other_methods">Other methods</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other methods"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Although the parameters of a regression model are usually estimated using the method of least squares, other methods which have been used include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bayesian_method" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayesian method">Bayesian methods</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_linear_regression" title="Bayesian linear regression">Bayesian linear regression</a></li>
<li>Percentage regression, for situations where reducing <i>percentage</i> errors is deemed more appropriate.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Least_absolute_deviations" title="Least absolute deviations">Least absolute deviations</a>, which is more robust in the presence of outliers, leading to <a href="/wiki/Quantile_regression" title="Quantile regression">quantile regression</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nonparametric_regression" title="Nonparametric regression">Nonparametric regression</a>, requires a large number of observations and is computationally intensive</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scenario_optimization" title="Scenario optimization">Scenario optimization</a>, leading to  <a href="/wiki/Interval_predictor_model" title="Interval predictor model">interval predictor models</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Software">Software</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regression_analysis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Software"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_statistical_software" title="List of statistical software">List of statistical software</a>.</div>
<p>All major statistical software packages perform <a href="/wiki/Least_squares" title="Least squares">least squares</a> regression analysis and inference. <a href="/wiki/Simple_linear_regression" title="Simple linear regression">Simple linear regression</a> and multiple regression using least squares can be done in some <a href="/wiki/Spreadsheet" title="Spreadsheet">spreadsheet</a> applications and on some calculators. While many statistical software packages can perform various types of nonparametric and robust regression, these methods are less standardized. Different software packages implement different methods, and a method with a given name may be implemented differently in different packages. Specialized regression software has been developed for use in fields such as survey analysis and neuroimaging.
</p>
